Health New England

Drug Formulary

Health New England Pharmacy Beneﬁt: 5 Tier Formulary
Health New England is committed to providing our members with access to safe and effective
medications. We cover most prescription products and a small number of non-prescription
products and medical supplies. Covered prescription products are divided into three tiers with
different member copays. Copays are applied toward the out-of-pocket maximum.
Copay Tiers
Health New England has three levels of copays (tiers) for medications. Medications are classified
into generic, brand/formulary, and brand/non-formulary tiers.
Generic/Tier 1: Includes mostly generic products which are approved by the FDA. These
products contain the same active ingredients as brand name products, are just as safe and
effective, and usually cost less. Note: In Massachusetts, pharmacists are required to fill
generic products unless your doctor orders the brand name by including “no substitution” on
the prescription.
Brand Formulary/Tier 2: Includes mostly brand/formulary products. These products are
marketed under a trademarked brand name, by one company, and do not have less expensive
generic equivalents. Brand/Formulary products are selected based on a review of the relative
safety, effectiveness and cost of the many FDA approved products on the market. Your copay for
Brand/Formulary products is higher than generic products, but lower than Brand/Non-Formulary
products.
Brand Non-Formulary/Tier 3: Includes mostly brand name products that are not a
Brand/Formulary product. These products are still covered, but at the highest copay level.
Health New England covers brand name products that have FDA approved generic equivalents
only if medical necessity has been shown. Your doctor may request prior authorization for a
brand name product by filling out a product request form and faxing it to Health New England
for review with documentation of medical necessity. Medical necessity includes, but is not
limited to, inadequate response to or allergic reaction to the generic(s) and failure of alternatives
in the product class.
Formulary Specialty/Tier 4: Formulary Specialty products (Tier 4) are selected based on a
review of the relative safety, effectiveness and cost of the many FDA-approved drugs on the
market.
Non-Formulary Specialty/Tier 5: Any brand name product that Health New England has not
selected as a Formulary Specialty product is a Non-Formulary Specialty product (Tier 5). This
category includes brand product that have formulary generic and brand alternatives. These
medications are still covered, but at the highest copay level.
Certain medications are covered with $0 copay (please note that deductible may apply). For the
most up-to-date list of medications available at $0 copay, please call Member Services at (413)
787-4004 or (800) 310-2835.

New Medications/Products
Brand name medications that are new to the market and existing medications with new FDA
approved indications are not added to the Health New England formulary immediately. There is
a minimum 6-month period after medications are approved by the FDA called the Clinical
Review Period (CRP). This applies to all new medications, including those dispensed at a retail
pharmacy, from a specialty pharmacy, in a provider’s office, or at an infusion suite.
Health New England does not cover medications during the clinical review period. If your
provider feels that it is medically necessary to prescribe this medication, he or she may request
an exception. If Health New England approves coverage of the medication during the clinical
review period, your copay will be 50% of the cost of the medication. At the end of the clinical
review period, Health New England may decide not to cover the medication and add it to the
exclusion list. If this happens, Health New England will not cover the medication after the
clinical review period. If Health New England does decide to cover the medication, a copay tier
will be assigned.
Compounded Medications
Health New England covers certain compounded medications. For questions regarding coverage,
please call Member Services at 413-787-4004 or 800-310-2835.
Maintenance Medications
Health New England allows members to receive a 90-day supply of maintenance medications at
participating retail pharmacies or via Optum home delivery. Certain benefit plans provide cost
savings using the Optum Home Delivery mail order benefit.
Specialty Medications
Health New England has a list of medications that are limited to being filled at a specialty
pharmacy. These medications must be filled at OptumRX Specialty Pharmacy or Baystate
Specialty Pharmacy.
Prescription Medication Limitations
Prior Authorization Program
Prior authorization for select prescription medications is required. Health New England’s
pharmacy benefit manager (PBM) performs prior authorization review using Health New
England approved criteria.
Step Therapy Program
Step therapy is an approach to medication management and is part of the Health New England
prior authorization program. Health New England requires you to first try certain drugs to treat
your medical condition (known as first line medications) before we will cover another drug for
that condition. For example, if Drug A (first line medication) and Drug B both treat your medical
condition, we may not cover Drug B unless you try Drug A first. If Drug A does not work for
you, we will then cover Drug B.

If you have a paid claim for a first line medication within the past 180 days, the step therapy
medication will be covered. If you have tried the first line medication outside of the 180-day
window, your provider may submit medical records to Health New England for review. The use
of samples of first line medications does not satisfy this requirement.
If your provider finds that it is medically necessary for you to use a step therapy medication
before trying a first line medication, he or she can request a prior authorization from Health New
England.
Health New England will inform you (or your employer if you are in a group plan) in writing
about medications added to the step therapy program via an amendment to your EOC. Health
New England Member Services can provide you with an updated list of step therapy
medications. Please call Member Services or visit our online formulary at healthnewengland.org.
Health New England’s Quantity Limit Program
All prescription medications in the United States are reviewed and approved by the Food and
Drug Administration (FDA). The FDA recommends quantity limits for prescribed medications
When a prescription is filled, it is electronically screened for several quality issues including
allergies, medication interactions and dosage limits.
Health New England sets quantity limits on most medications to follow the FDA daily dosing
guide. If a prescription is written for over this limit, your provider will need to contact Health
New England for a prior authorization.
Review Process for Quantity Limitations, Step Therapy, or Exceptions
Your physician may ask us to review a request by completing our Medication Request Form
(MRF). This form can be found on healthnewengland.org or by calling Member Services at 413787-4004 or 800-310-2835.
Changes to Health New England’s Formulary
Health New England’s formulary is available via the website: Healthnewengland.org. A copy
may also be requested by contacting Member Services. Periodically, Health New England makes
changes to the formulary and will send these changes to you (or to your employer if you are in a
group plan) at least 60 days in advance. If a generic equivalent becomes available for any brand
name medication on the formulary, the brand name medication will automatically not be covered
unless medical necessity is established. Each year, Health New England sends a reminder to our
providers about where they can find the Health New England formulary and will include
formulary changes during the year in newsletters for members and providers.
Questions
If you have any questions about your prescription medications, please speak with your doctor. If
you have questions about the formulary or your coverage, please call Member Services at 413787-4004 or 800-310-2835 (TTY: 711), Monday through Friday, 8:00 a.m. to 6:00 p.m., or visit
our website at healthnewengland.org.
